  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5a240284-c0dc-4110-b8e2-075ac91b2ff9'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer17599378689569622005">Leland Gaunt opens a new shop in Castle Rock called Needful Things. Anyone who enters his store finds the object of his or her lifelong dreams and desires: a prized baseball card, a healing amulet. In addition to a token payment, Gaunt requests that each person perform a little "deed," usually a seemingly innocent prank played on someone else from town. These practical jok</span>
  <span id="freeText17599378689569622005" style="display:none">Leland Gaunt opens a new shop in Castle Rock called Needful Things. Anyone who enters his store finds the object of his or her lifelong dreams and desires: a prized baseball card, a healing amulet. In addition to a token payment, Gaunt requests that each person perform a little "deed," usually a seemingly innocent prank played on someone else from town. These practical jokes cascade out of control and soon the entire town is doing battle with itself. Only Sheriff Alan Pangborn suspects that Gaunt is behind the population's increasingly violent behavior.</span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/32461006-kevin"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_100x100-c7bfe730633c9983e27caaa66a8e244a.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/32461006-kevin">Kevin</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The simple answer to your question is that we will never know unless he writes Stephen King writes a follow up to this novel. I too would love to read<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The simple answer to your question is that we will never know unless he writes Stephen King writes a follow up to this novel. I too would love to read more about the Leland Gaunt and what he does with all the souls he has collected. All the author tells us is that collecting souls is not the main mission. Gaunt above and beyond all else simply wants to entertain himself. He is certainly one of my favorite characters in the SK universe and is more than entertaining. <br /><br />Now the uncut answer to your question. ow the Uncut answer to your question.... Stephen King is one of my favorite authors. His biggest weaknesses as a writer is probably the fact that he seems to be unable to write endings which are satisfying. This issue is probably most glaring in his novel The Stand. Although I am not familiar with the uncut version but the original is just over 800 pages long and kept me turning pages until the sun came up on more than a few occasions. I've read it three times over the last thirty or so years yet the ending had me wondering if it was not some kind of practical joke. In spite of this I still found it necessary to read it three times in the last thirty years or so. I will not spoil it if you have not read it but, well, it was one of the most pathetic endings to any novel can think of with the exception of probably half a dozen other Stephen King novels can think of. King takes this weakness to new heights in the Dark Tower series which contains six fairly thick novels not including the first of the series which is fairly short. I loved the entire series but the end of the series was much like the end to many of his novels in that it just ended flat in my opinion. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer847638258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10862368146691081814">As Jeff turned to go into Needful Things, he bumped into a woman wearing a <s>dazed</s> determined expression, who was hurrying out the door, clutching a stuffed warthog. Entering the store, he was greeted by a tinkling bell and what appeared to be the shop owner, walking toward him with an outstretched hand. Jeff’s first instinct was to back away in revulsion, but he extended his hand and felt a wave of nausea sweep over him.<br/><br/>“I’m Leland Gaunt and welcome to my humble establishment. I’ve just opened to</span>
  <span id="freeText10862368146691081814" style="display:none">As Jeff turned to go into Needful Things, he bumped into a woman wearing a <s>dazed</s> determined expression, who was hurrying out the door, clutching a stuffed warthog. Entering the store, he was greeted by a tinkling bell and what appeared to be the shop owner, walking toward him with an outstretched hand. Jeff’s first instinct was to back away in revulsion, but he extended his hand and felt a wave of nausea sweep over him.<br /><br />“I’m Leland Gaunt and welcome to my humble establishment. I’ve just opened today and I haven’t gotten all my goods unpacked, but you’re welcome to look around.”<br /><br />Gaunt had the strangest shade of green eyes that Jeff had ever seen. It was as if Jeff was staring into a bowl of spinach.<br /><br />As Jeff walked around the store he noticed that, no matter where he turned his head, Mr. Gaunt never left his peripheral vision.<br /><br />Looking at a glass case, Jeff noticed a paper with writing. It was the cleverest, best written, funniest review he had ever read. And it was a review of the book he was currently reading. Why if Jeff put this out on Goodreads, he’d get thousands of “likes”. Thousands.<br /><br />Gaunt appeared over his left shoulder. “That is something, isn’t it? I just got that in today.”<br /><br />Jeff felt he had to have it. Maybe tens of thousands of likes. “It is pretty good. How much do you want for it?”<br /><br />Gaunt smiled. His teeth reminded Jeff of gravestones. “Well, how much money do you have?”<br /><br />How much money do I have? Jeff checked his wallet. “Only four dollars.”<br /><br />Gaunt gave him his best shark-like smile and said, “What a coincidence, that’s what I’m selling it for.”<br /><br />As Gaunt pulled it out of the case, Jeff could have sworn the page was a shopping list, but once Gaunt handed it over, he saw it was his precious review. The greatest review he had ever read.<br /><br />“By the way Jeff, (Jeff didn’t remember telling Gaunt his name), I’d like you to play a small prank on someone…"<br /></span>

<div id="review_2334706692" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2334706692" />
    <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus"><img alt="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588320656p2/78485297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2334706692?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus">Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus?shelf=king-stephen">king-stephen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2334706692" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12573660475897211131">An interesting sociocultural study about the group dynamics of small towns, executed with interesting experiments regarding greed, trying to trigger archaic primate reactions, and manipulating the microeconomics with difficult to grasp, metaphysical values that just subjectively exist. Cool stock market and economic system criticism, by the way.<br/> <br/>Also a monument of pop culture history emphasizing and demonstrating the importance of staying away from all that freaking people, neighbors, and friend</span>
  <span id="freeText12573660475897211131" style="display:none">An interesting sociocultural study about the group dynamics of small towns, executed with interesting experiments regarding greed, trying to trigger archaic primate reactions, and manipulating the microeconomics with difficult to grasp, metaphysical values that just subjectively exist. Cool stock market and economic system criticism, by the way.<br /> <br />Also a monument of pop culture history emphasizing and demonstrating the importance of staying away from all that freaking people, neighbors, and friends, because their dark desires, mental illnesses, and pure evilness is nothing for the faint of heart, especially if they can´t even understand harmless, little jokes among friends from the same street.<br /> <br />There are some soft spoilers, but I am too lazy to differentiate and add a simple template, sorry. I mean, deal with it, what am I, a nebulous new shop owner?<br /> <br />There it is, the neighborhood, friendly greetings, short waste of time, accumulating to hours and days, small talk chats, and, depending on states of mind, subconsciously or hardly to suppress willing to mutilate, kill, or sleep with someone, not always in that order. The sadism, gruesomeness, and envy naturally growing in any good human society can already be brought to light or misused by demagogues, sociopaths, salesmen, and politicians, but add a grain of dark conventional and mind magic to the mix and perfection is sure. <br /> <br />It´s not as if a demon would have to try hard to turn angels into devils, it´s a bit more of playing with snowballs on top of a huge mountain when avalanche alert level is at ridiculous heights. I live in an alpine country, better don´t do it (obviously) and especially don´t get caught, the souls could haunt you, not to speak of the cops. Philosophizing about if there is inherent evil in all humans, if it´s a decision of choice, if turning people evil is evil or just natural, and, most important, what new products and services may wait to be enjoyed, are underlying ideas. Focus on that last one, who cares about the other stuff, consume. <br /> <br />The McGuffins are delicious in this one, you should try! I´ll ship them to you for free and add a 20 Euro, Dollar, or whatever gift card for the online shop of your choice on the dark web. You would be crazy to not agree to this amazing offer, I must be really bonkers to do this. Never look a gift horse in the mouth, what could go wrong. It´s not as if each positive, free offer comes with terrible butterfly effects, chain reactions, hidden problems, and bloody anarchy. That I am secretly filming and streaming on the same dark web you got that stuff from, to add ads and get rich with monetarization.<br /> <br />I´m a bit wondering how quickly something like this would escalate in real life, but sadly no reality tv show format would dare to do it because of stupid laws, boring human rights, and this damned rarity of personified devils and haunted magic artifacts. They could cooperate with museums, get haunted objects, blood gold, torture equipment, and work together with private collectors who could give items on loan from their private collections to get this thing started. <br /> <br />Seriously, I´ve already said this before, I am a cold, reasonable person, but for some strange reason I don´t visit haunted, strange places where terrible things happened, sometimes over centuries, or, would be a bit expensive too, collect old, haunted, objects to decorate my house and bedroom with. No making sandwiches with the strangely glowing obsidian blade used for human sacrifice to celebrate whatever unspeakable, and difficult to pronounce too, god, also a bit unhygienic, yuck, say hello to my little OCD mysophobia hybrid. Whoever has the same „I am so sophisticated“ excuse and self-deceit should think why we are such wimps if there is really nothing to fear. Hint: Science knows nothing about some essential fields that would be important to go up to 100 percent certainly nothing terrifying, although we don´t know.<br /> <br />Oh, and don´t buy in small local shops owned by creepy men with too good to be true offers, just in big retail store chains to protect yourself or, even better, online. There are rumors that AIs are trained with algorithms to detect paranormal activities before they even happen, predictive psi protection against perverted ghosts, ghouls, dwarfs, succubi, and incubi and money back offers if one gets still haunted. Hopefully, the evil, small, one man, dark magic shops never grow big and dominate the world market, that would be terrible.<br /><br />Tropes show how literature is conceptualized and created and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/NeedfulThings">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12573660475897211131" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_813518642" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/813518642" />
    <a title="Gregor Xane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2165551-gregor-xane"><img alt="Gregor Xane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383011083p2/2165551.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/813518642?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gregor Xane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gregor Xane" href="/user/show/2165551-gregor-xane">Gregor Xane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2165551-gregor-xane?shelf=ha-horror-challenge-2014">ha-horror-challenge-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2165551-gregor-xane?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer813518642" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5677736496550210519">Mr. King likes to tell stories about people getting trapped. He's got one about a guy trapped in a bedroom. He's got a whole bunch of these stories, really. He's got people trapped inside a car, in a gas station, a classroom, a grocery store, a hotel, on an island, a city under a giant force field. I'm pretty sure he's got one about a lady handcuffed to a bed for the whole book. I'm just going from memory here. He's probably got a lot more.<br/><br/>In <i>Needful Things</i>, the entire town of Castle Rock is tra</span>
  <span id="freeText5677736496550210519" style="display:none">Mr. King likes to tell stories about people getting trapped. He's got one about a guy trapped in a bedroom. He's got a whole bunch of these stories, really. He's got people trapped inside a car, in a gas station, a classroom, a grocery store, a hotel, on an island, a city under a giant force field. I'm pretty sure he's got one about a lady handcuffed to a bed for the whole book. I'm just going from memory here. He's probably got a lot more.<br /><br />In <i>Needful Things</i>, the entire town of Castle Rock is trapped by their possessions. Its citizens are punished mercilessly for 700+ pages with some special brand of evil that feeds off the sin of imbuing bric-à-brac with sentimental value.<br /><br />Admittedly, I'm oversimplifying the plot of this book quite a bit. But <i>Needful Things</i> is just a morality tale at its core, a boldfaced warning about materialism. The message of the book seems to boil down to something we all heard as kids, mom saying that you don't <i>need</i> those roller skates, you just <i>want</i> them.<br /><br />But to say that this is <i>only</i> a simple morality tale really does this book a disservice. It's got all the things I like in a King book: suspense, action, gore, folksy humor (the cruel and the crude varieties), characters you can identify with, protagonists you care about, insane people and perverts, monsters and great big explosions. Most importantly, it's got a great villain. Our bad guy, Leland Gaunt, isn't subtle, he chews up the scenery at every turn, but he's exactly what this novel calls for. Done well (and King does them very well), comic book villains are the best kind. All right, maybe just the most fun to read about.<br /><br />And, yes, this book had some of the Stephen King things I don't like so much. I feel sometimes King is writing down to his characters, like he'll create a character just for the sake of mockery. Lester Pratt, the goody two-shoes, Christian 'boy scout' character in this book is a prime example. I would be willing to bet that no one ever--no matter how repressed and/or brainwashed, sheltered, or close-minded--ever, ever had an internal monologue that's featured the celebratory phrase "rooty toot toot" <i>repeatedly</i> while thinking about the prospect of getting some pussy.<br /><br />King also has a tendency to veer into some rather cloying, almost treacly, Garrison Keillor territory, and in this book the opening and closing are perhaps the most nauseating examples of this that I've personally encountered.<br /><br />And then, like with many of King's novels, we have the borderline <i>deus ex machina</i> ending.<br /><br />Now, I know what you're thinking:<br /><br /><i>Wow, it seemed like there for a minute you were saying you like Stephen King. But now it seems like you're being rather hard on the guy.</i><br /><br />But, you see, the thing is, Stephen King is sort of like the President of the United States of America. (Bear with me here.) The people you hear bitching about the President the most, the people who are the hardest on him, seem to always be the very same people who voted him into office. I've read over thirty books by Stephen King. So, in my mind, that pretty much means I voted that son-of-a-bitch into office over <i>thirty fucking times!</i> <br /><br />I'll say what I want.<br /><br />And now you're probably asking, <i>would you vote for that son-of-a-bitch again?</i><br /><br />No question.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5677736496550210519" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444707878" href="/book/show/10493548-needful-things">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1570613969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16477594586749605747">“You’ve been here before.”<br/><br/>Nothing. beats. King’s. small. town. stories. And that’s a fact!<br/><br/>A criminally underrated King novel (outside of bookstagram anyway), Needful Things is a firecracker. My paperback is 900+ pages and at no point did my attention or interest wane. This book is pretty much sheer chaos from beginning to end and I was LIVING for it!!<br/><br/>The premise is simple. There’s a new store in Castle Rock, and no matter what your heart’s deepest desire is, it’s in stock. And the price is exact</span>
  <span id="freeText16477594586749605747" style="display:none">“You’ve been here before.”<br /><br />Nothing. beats. King’s. small. town. stories. And that’s a fact!<br /><br />A criminally underrated King novel (outside of bookstagram anyway), Needful Things is a firecracker. My paperback is 900+ pages and at no point did my attention or interest wane. This book is pretty much sheer chaos from beginning to end and I was LIVING for it!!<br /><br />The premise is simple. There’s a new store in Castle Rock, and no matter what your heart’s deepest desire is, it’s in stock. And the price is exactly what you can afford. You just gotta play a little prank for Leland Gaunt to get your hands on it...<br /><br />King’s ability to create a fictional town with an entire cast of real, distinguishable characters will never cease to amaze me. The way that Gaunt plays the town members off each other, demonstrating how dangerous materialism can be, is such a genius idea, and you can really feel that King is having an absolute blast writing this one! And I had a blast reading it. I was downright CACKLING at some parts - the battle between Cora Rusk and Myra Evans over Elvis artefacts was a highlight for me, as well as a character literally shitting on a photograph of someone’s mother!! I told you this one is CHAOS!<br /><br />In terms of characters, I love Sheriff Alan Pangborn and you really gotta feel for his heartbreaking backstory. You can see why he and Polly Chalmers are drawn to each other, they have both been through a lot of pain and find some solace in each other. Although one of their sex scenes was just... uncomfortable for me to read. I don’t know why, but I just imagine 70 year old King writing this and it makes me feel icky - even though this was written back in the early 90s.<br /><br />ANYWHO, absolutely loved this reread. Might have to reshuffle my top 10 King yet again... 5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16477594586749605747" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_789554749" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/789554749" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/789554749?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=kitten-squisher">kitten-squisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer789554749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16227998476791331253">A store has opened in the Maine town of Castle Rock, a store selling objects a person most desires, at a price the buyer can afford. But are the goods worth the cost? Can Sheriff Alan Pangborn get to the bottom of Leland Gaunt and his Needful Things before he falls prey to the madness that's gripping the town?<br/><br/>In what originally was intended to be its final appearance, Castle Rock goes out with a bang in this Stephen King tome. <br/><br/>It reads like a love letter to Castle Rock at times. I caught referen</span>
  <span id="freeText16227998476791331253" style="display:none">A store has opened in the Maine town of Castle Rock, a store selling objects a person most desires, at a price the buyer can afford. But are the goods worth the cost? Can Sheriff Alan Pangborn get to the bottom of Leland Gaunt and his Needful Things before he falls prey to the madness that's gripping the town?<br /><br />In what originally was intended to be its final appearance, Castle Rock goes out with a bang in this Stephen King tome. <br /><br />It reads like a love letter to Castle Rock at times. I caught references to The Dark Half, Cujo, Sun Dog, The Body, and I think Cycle of the Werewolf. Ace Merrill and Alan Pangborn are the only characters I remember from other books but I'm sure there were probably others.<br /><br />The story starts off slow as, one by one, the citizens of Castle Rock fall prey to Leland Gaunt's charms, buying his trinkets for whatever cash they have on them and doing pranks for him. These pranks are as custom tailored to the victim as the trinkets he sells and soon the denizens of Castle Rock are fuming at one another. Once things escalate to the point of violence, there's no turning back, making Needful Things very hard to put down for such a heavy book.<br /><br />There's not a lot more I can tell without giving things away. Alan Pangborn could have been a Gunslinger in another life and his relationship with Polly was pretty well done. Ace Merrill was a world class douche and fell into the #2 bad guy role pretty well. I thought Needful Things took the gossip and cattiness that's a staple of small town life and turned the dial up until it broke off. <br /><br />Things I'm still pondering:<br />- Was the spider that appeared near the end a relative of the spider from It, only feeding on pain instead of fear?<br />- Are Leland Gaunt and Randall Flag the same person?<br />- What happened to Castle Rock after the conflagration at the end?<br /><br />Needful Things is like cooking a pot roast in a crock pot. It starts out slow, begins to simmer, and is a churning cauldron of deliciousness by the end. Four out of five stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16227998476791331253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3007443214" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780340952764" href="/book/show/1278248.Needful_Things">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3007443214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3900821069185660749"><b>Needful Things, Stephen King</b><br/><br/>Leland Gaunt opens a new shop in Castle Rock called Needful Things. Anyone who enters his store finds the object of his or her lifelong dreams and desires: a prized baseball card, a healing amulet. In addition to a token payment, Gaunt requests that each person perform a little "deed," usually a seemingly innocent prank played on someone else from town. <br/><br/>These practical jokes cascade out of control and soon the entire town is doing battle with itself. Only Sheriff Alan</span>
  <span id="freeText3900821069185660749" style="display:none"><b>Needful Things, Stephen King</b><br /><br />Leland Gaunt opens a new shop in Castle Rock called Needful Things. Anyone who enters his store finds the object of his or her lifelong dreams and desires: a prized baseball card, a healing amulet. In addition to a token payment, Gaunt requests that each person perform a little "deed," usually a seemingly innocent prank played on someone else from town. <br /><br />These practical jokes cascade out of control and soon the entire town is doing battle with itself. Only Sheriff Alan Pangborn suspects that Gaunt is behind the population's increasingly violent behavior.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز دهم ماه اکتبر سال 2014میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: چیزهای ضروری؛ نویسنده: استیفن کینگ ؛ مترجم: سهیلا فرزین‌نژاد؛ تهران روشنگران و مطالعات زنان‏‫،‫1391؛ در 778ص؛ ‬‬شابک 9789641940968؛ موضوع داستانهای ترسناک از نویسندگان ایالات متحده امریکا - سده 20م<br /><br />باز شدن یک فروشگاه تازه بنام «چیزهای ضروری» در یک شهر کوچک به نام «کاسل» در ایالت «مین»، جوششی در شهر پدیدار می‌کند؛ مدیر فروشگاه یک مرد میانسال خوش چهره، و آقامنش به نام «لیلاند گرانت» است، که به نظر میرسد همیشه چیزی در فروشگاهش دارد، تا مناسب خواسته ی یکی از اهالی شهر باشد؛ چیزهای متنوع، از بلیت «مسابقه‌ ی بیسبال» گرفته، تا «چوب ماهیگیری»؛ اما آیا هدف واقعی او جلب رضایت مردم شهر است، یا هدف خبیثانه‌ ی دیگری، در پشت این چهره‌ ی به ظاهر آرام پنهان است؟ <br /><br />نقل نمونه متن: «تو پیش از اینم اینجا بودی: آره جونم، معلومه؛ من هیچ وقت قیافه ی کسی رو فراموش نمیکنم؛ بیا اینجا، بذار دستتو فشار بدم! بذار یه چیزی رو بهت بگم؛ حتی پیش از اینکه صورتتو خوب ببینم، از راه رفتنت شناختمت؛ دیگه هیچ روزی بهتر از اینو نمیتونستی برای برگشتن به «کاسل راک» پیدا کنی؛ راستی شهرعجیبی نیست؟ فصل شکار همین روزا شروع میشه؛ احمقا تو جنگل به طرف هر چیزی که تکون بخوره، تیر در میکنن، تازه جلیقه ی نارنجی تندشونم نمیپوشن؛ بعدشم برف و بوران تموم میشه، ولی اون مال بعده؛ حالا فعلا اکتبره، اینجا تو «راک»، ما میذاریم اکتبر هر چی دلش میخواد طول بکشه؛ به نظر من این بهترین وقت ساله؛ بهار اینجا قشنگه، اما من همیشه اکتبرو به «مه» ترجیح میدم؛ «ماین غربی» یه قسمت از ایالته، که وقتی تابستون تموم میشه، و اون مردمیکه لب دریاچه، یا بالای «ویو»، کلبه ی ییلاقی دارن، برمیگردن «نیویورک» و «ماساچوست»، دیگه پاک فراموش میشه؛ مردم اینجا اونا رو تماشا میکنن، که هرسال میآن و میرن؛ سلام، سلام، سلام؛ خدافظ، خدافظ، خدافظ؛ <br /><br />وقتی که میآن خوبه، چون دلارهای شهرشونو میآرن، اما وقتی هم که میرن خوبه، چون موقع اومدن دردسرای شهرشونم میآرن؛ منم بیشتر میخوام درباره ی دردسرا با تو حرف بزنم؛ میتونی یه کم پیش من بشینی؟ اینجا روی پله های جای ارکستر، خوبه! آفتاب گرمه و از اینجا، درست وسط میدون اجتماعات شهر، میتونیم تقریبا تموم مرکز شهرو ببینیم؛ فقط باید تراشه ها رو بپایی، همین؛ این پله ها باید سمباده بخورن، و بعدشم رنگ بشن؛ این کارم باید «هیو پریست» بکنه، اما «هیو» هنوز وقتشو پیدا نکرده؛ میدونی، عرق میخوره؛ این دیگه یه راز نیست؛ تو «کاسل راک»، اسرار رو میشه نگه داشت، و همین طورم هست، منتها باید خیلی سعی کنی تا موفق بشی، بیشتر ماها میدونیم که از اون زمانهایی که «هیو» میونه اش با کار سخت خوب بود، خیلی گذشته<br /><br />چی گفتی؟ آهان! اون! میگم ها، پسر – این خودش کاریه ها؛ این همه اعلامیه تو همه جای شهر چسبوندن؛ من فکر میکنم «وندا همفیل» (که شوهرش «دان» فروشگاه «همفیل» رو میگردونه) خودش تنهایی بیشتر اونا رو چسبونده؛ از روی اون میله بکن، بدش به من؛ خجالت نکش، تازه از اولش هم کسی حق نداشته که روی جای ارکستر میدون اجتماعات، اعلامیه بچسبونه؛ لعنت خدا! اینو نیگا گن، میبینی؟ <br /><br />همین بالاش چاپ زدن «تاس و ابلیس»؛ حروف قرمز درشت، که ازشون دود میآد بیرون، و انگاری با پست سفارشی از «توفت» اومدن اینجا؛ هه! فکر کنم اگه کسی راس راسی ندونه این شهر، چه جای کوچولوی خواب آلودیه، فکر میکنه که جدی جدی، ما داریم فنا میشیم؛ اما میدونی توی یه شهر اینقدری، بعضی وقتها چه طوری همه چی گنده میشه؛ و جناب کشیش «ویلی» این دفعه دیگه حتما کک به تنبونش افتاده، هیچ شکی دراینباره نیست؛ کلیساها تو شهرای کوچیک…؛ خب فکر کنم، مجبور نیستم که بهت بگم، وضع از چه قراره؛ یه جورایی با هم کنار میآن، اما خب هیچ وقت از همدیگه راضی نیستن؛ یه مدتی همه چی آروم پیش میره، و بعدش یه هو جنجالی به پا میشه<br /><br />گرچه این دفعه جنجال تقریبا شدید بود، با کلی دلخوری، میدونی «کاتولیکها» دارن اونور شهر، تو تالار شوالیه های «کلمبوس»، یه چیزی راه میاندازن، که اسمشو گذاشتن «کازینو نایت»؛ شنیدم پنج شنبه ی آخر هر ماه؛ سودش هم قراره که برای تعمیر سقف کلیسای «بانوی آبهای آرام» ما مصرف بشه؛ اگه از طرف «کاسل ویو» اومده باشی تو شهر، حتما اونو سر راهت دیدی؛ کلیسای کوچولوی قشنگیه، مگه نه؟ «کازینو نایت» اولش فکر «پدر برایهام» بود، اما دخترهای «ایزابلا» در واقع کسایی بودن، که فکرو گرفتن و رفتن دنبالش، مخصوصا «بتسی ویگ»؛<br /><br />فکر کنم خوشش میآد که چسبونترین لباس مشکیشو بپوشه، و سر میز بیست و یک، ورق بده، یا صفحه ی رولتو بچرخونه، و بگه «پولاتونو بذارین، خانمها و آقایون، لطفا پولاتونو بذارین»؛ وای که فکر میکنم همشون یه جورایی از این ایده خوششون میآد؛ فقط سرِ چندرغازه، بیضرره، اما خوب فرقی نمیکنه، یه کمی هم به نظرشون شریرانه میآد؛ فقط به نظر «عالیجناب ویلی» این موضوع بیضرر نمیآد، و از نظر اون و جماعتش خیلی بیشتر از یه کم شریرانه ست؛ راستشو بخوای «عالیجناب ویلیام رز» اسم اصلیشه، هیچ وقتم از «پدر برایهام» خوشش نمیاومده، «پدر برایهام» هم علاقه ای به اون نداره؛ در واقع اول از همه «پدر برایهام» بود، که اسم «کشتی بخار ویلی» رو روی «عالیجناب رز» گذاشت، و خود «عالیجناب ویلی» هم این موضوعو میدونه؛ قبلاً هم جرقه هایی بین این دوتا جادوگر قبیله، رد و بدل شده بود، اما این مسئاله ی «کازینو نایت»، دیگه از جرقه یه کمی بیشتره؛ گمون کنم بتونی بهش بگی آتیش تند؛<br /><br />وقتی «ویلی» شنید که کاتولیکها میخوان یه شبو تو تالار «شوالیه های کلمبوس»، به قمار بگذرونن، کم مونده بود از عصبانیت اون کله ی تیز و کوچولوشو، بکوبه به طاق؛ اون اعلامیه های «تاس و ابلیس» رو هم، با پول خودش درست کرد، و «وندا همفیل» با دوستای دوره ی خیاطیش، اونارو به همه جا چسبوندن؛ از اونوقت به بعدم تنها جایی که «کاتولیکها» و «بابتیستها» با هم حرف میزنن، ستون «نامه ها»ی هفته نامه ی کوچیک ماست، که اونجا هم به همدیگه بد و بیراه میگن، و پرت و پلا، بار هم میکنن، و به همدیگه میگن، که جاشون ته جهنمه؛ <br /><br />اونجا رو نیگا کن، خودت میفهمی من چی میگم؛ اون «نان روبرتس» بود، که همین الان از بانک دراومد بیرون؛ صاحاب غذاخوری «نانه»؛ فکر کنم الان که «پوپ مریل» به اون بازار مکاره ی بزرگ، تو آسمونا رفته، «نان» تقریبا پولدارترین آدم شهره؛ از وقتی هم که «هکتور» یه توله ی کوچولو بود، «نان» «بابتیست» بوده؛ از اونطرف هم «ال گندرون بزرگ» داره میآد؛ یارو اونقدر کاتولیکه که «پاپ» پیش اون کاشر به نظر میآد، بهترین دوستش هم «جانی برایهام» ایرلندیه؛ حالا، خوب بپا! میبینی چه جوری دماغاشونو بالا گرفتن؟ هی هی، خنده دار نیست؟ من سر یه دلار به یه دونات، باهات شرط میبندم درست جایی که اون دوتا، از بغل همدیگه رد شدن، درجه حرارت بیست درجه پایین افتاد؛<br /><br />به قول مادرم، آدما از همه بیشتر خوش میگذرونن، غیر از اسبها، و اونام نمیتونن؛ حالا اون ورو بپا؛ ماشین گشت کلانترو میبینی که دم پیاده رو نزدیک مغازه ی «ویدیو» پارک شده؟ اونم «جان لاپوینت» که توی مغازه اس؛ قراره مواظب کسایی باشه که تند میرونن، آخه میدونی مرکز شهر محدوده ی سرعت کمه، مخصوصا وقتی که بچه های مدرسه میریزن بیرون، اما اگه دستتو سایبون چشمت کنی، و درست نیگا کنی، میبینی کاری که واقعا داره میکنه اینه که، زل زده به یه عکس، که از توی کیفش درآورده؛ از اینجا نمیتونم اونو ببینم، اما عکسیه که تقریبا یه سال پیش «اندی کلاترباک» از «جان» و «سالی راتکلیف»، تو نمایشگاه ایالتی «فرایبرگ» گرفت؛ تو اون عکس، بازوی «جانی» دور شونه ی «سالیه» و «سالی» هم یه «خرس عروسکی» رو، که «جانی» تو سالن تیراندازی برنده شده، دستش گرفته، و هردوشونم اونقدر خوشن، که نزدیکه از خنده روده بر بشن؛ اما اون مال اون روزا بود، نه الان؛ اینطور که میگن این روزا «سالی» با «لستر پرات» مربی تربیت بدنی دبیرستان، نامزد کرده؛ اونم مث «سالی» یه «بابتیست» خالص و پروپا قرصه؛ «جان» هنوز از شوک از دست دادن «سالی» بیرون نیومده؛ دیدی چه آهی کشید؟ اون سر این مسئاله خیلی ناراحت شده؛ فقط مردی که هنوز عاشقه (یا فکر میکنه که هست) میتونه آهی به این عمیقی بکشه؛ ...؛»؛ پایان نقل<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 30/07/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3900821069185660749" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2547059006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4845512264740971506">If something sounds too good to be true, it probably is. This is the basic premise of <i>Needful Things</i>, one of the strangest Stephen King books I've ever read starring a really well-developed antagonist and a great balance of horror and fantasy. The story seems simple enough, a typical town sheriff pitted against Leland Gaunt, the mysterious and creepy owner of a shop that gives the citizens of Castle Rock anything they want for no price at all - but of course, <i>everything</i> has a price, and the peop</span>
  <span id="freeText4845512264740971506" style="display:none">If something sounds too good to be true, it probably is. This is the basic premise of <i>Needful Things</i>, one of the strangest Stephen King books I've ever read starring a really well-developed antagonist and a great balance of horror and fantasy. The story seems simple enough, a typical town sheriff pitted against Leland Gaunt, the mysterious and creepy owner of a shop that gives the citizens of Castle Rock anything they want for no price at all - but of course, <i>everything</i> has a price, and the people who don't ask why are left to regret it later. As a strange bout of madness grips the town and things start to get dangerous, the book takes a very sinister turn.<br /><br />If you've ever watched the 1990's show <i>Eerie Indiana</i>'s episode featuring a sinister investor who turns a small town shop into a hub of madness for desperate shoppers, or if you've ever watched <i>Gremlins</i>, you'll definitely like the kind of spooky store atmosphere <i>Needful Things</i> casts out. Stephen King crafts brilliant characters as usual, and though the Maine setting is a bit old considering it's chosen for almost all his books, the plot itself and the surprising events which unfold are definitely worth it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4845512264740971506" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28419239-needful-things">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27544490-annemarie?shelf=read-in-german">read-in-german</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2558947899" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3429710378317690725"> <b>Actual reading: 3.5🌟</b><br/><br/>As always with King, this was a very entertaining and suspenseful read the whole way through. However, somehow I just didn't connect as much to the characters as I usually do, which is why I cannot bring myself to give the full five stars. The plot itself was super interesting and I loved all the mysterious things that happened. There is also no shortage on gruesome scenes, so reading this during the spooky October time was definitely the right decision.<br/><br/>However, as I mention</span>
  <span id="freeText3429710378317690725" style="display:none"> <b>Actual reading: 3.5🌟</b><br /><br />As always with King, this was a very entertaining and suspenseful read the whole way through. However, somehow I just didn't connect as much to the characters as I usually do, which is why I cannot bring myself to give the full five stars. The plot itself was super interesting and I loved all the mysterious things that happened. There is also no shortage on gruesome scenes, so reading this during the spooky October time was definitely the right decision.<br /><br />However, as I mentioned, the characters just didn't quite appeal to me this time around. I found them interesting for the time being, but none of them truly stuck in my mind for long (which is usually the case whenever I read a book by King).<br />I'm someone who finds good characters more important than an exciting plot, so the fact that I didn't feel close to the characters bothered me a lot. If you're someone who cares more about a plot, I'm sure you will love this book, because the story on its own is unique and quite clever. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3429710378317690725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer570510285" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12229956459011938692">Re-read 11/17/20:<br/><br/>Just sitting back to re-read Needful Things and I was struck by how odd this novel is now, when all Needful Things seem to take the character of toilet paper and gyms.<br/><br/>I just had to think of Gaunt sitting us down to sign up for a 6-month membership, a pass to a bar, or a pack of Costco bum rolls. It's a bargain, you know! Never more than you can afford!!!<br/><br/>Yes. Indeed. And the pranks are all political.<br/><br/><br/>It's still a classic King novel! :) We're not any wiser, that's for sure.<br/><br/><br/>Original</span>
  <span id="freeText12229956459011938692" style="display:none">Re-read 11/17/20:<br /><br />Just sitting back to re-read Needful Things and I was struck by how odd this novel is now, when all Needful Things seem to take the character of toilet paper and gyms.<br /><br />I just had to think of Gaunt sitting us down to sign up for a 6-month membership, a pass to a bar, or a pack of Costco bum rolls. It's a bargain, you know! Never more than you can afford!!!<br /><br />Yes. Indeed. And the pranks are all political.<br /><br /><br />It's still a classic King novel! :) We're not any wiser, that's for sure.<br /><br /><br />Original Review:<br /><br />With this tome of Stephen King small town horror, I'm constantly amazed that I had missed picking this up and geeking out over it when it first came out.<br /><br />I'm certain that I would have. It has all the things I'd been learning to geek out about with his general horror universe, including Cthulhu references, homages to his previous works including events and characters, all of them strung up as if on a map of homicide victims on a perp board, and of course, Castle Rock, itself.<br /><br />Castle Rock Entertainment, indeed. This is the grand blowout of the town, with evil creeping in and changing all of its residents from a patina of middle-class respectability and Rockwellian charm into roving bands of gleeful murderers with very dark hearts.<br /><br />And can we really blame it entirely upon Antique Madness? Roadshow Antiques? That equally weird craze of the early '90s, turned EVIL? Or was it just Mr. Gaunt, aka (Flagg, maybe?) stirring up loads of crap? Nah, it's just the greed and pride of humanity, stoked in just the right way, and that's what Stephen King is really known for.<br /><br />His supernatural aspects are generally underplayed and always in direct support of deep characterizations, of twisting flawed people into even more atrocious examples of humanity, with usually only a few semi-heroic survivors at the end that *sometimes* manage to make it through the fire.<br /><br />This novel is a shining example of all this, taking all the best simmering-pot boil-over of 'Salem's Lot, the twisted madness of Tommyknockers, and throwing in an epic battle of two older ladies eviscerating each other in broad daylight on the street. :)<br /><br />Truly a charming novel. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12229956459011938692" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3393073648" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3393073648" />
    <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten"><img alt="Jeffrey Keeten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301087352p2/3427339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3393073648?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeffrey Keeten" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten">Jeffrey Keeten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780670839537" href="/book/show/411204.Needful_Things">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3393073648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18353262481124062382"><b>It was his Sandy Koufax card.<br/><br/>“And he was not going to give it up.<br/><br/>No way, uh-uh <i>negatory</i>.<br/><br/><i>Then you better finish paying for it,</i> a voice deep in his mind whispered.<br/><br/>He would. No problem there. He didn’t think the thing he was supposed to do was exactly nice, but he was pretty sure it wasn’t anything totally gross, either. Just a...a…<br/><br/><i>Just a prank,</i> a voice whispered in his mind, and he saw the eyes of Mr. Gaunt--dark blue, like the sea on a clear day, and strangely soothing. <i>That’s all. Just a little </i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText18353262481124062382" style="display:none"><b>It was his Sandy Koufax card.<br /><br />“And he was not going to give it up.<br /><br />No way, uh-uh <i>negatory</i>.<br /><br /><i>Then you better finish paying for it,</i> a voice deep in his mind whispered.<br /><br />He would. No problem there. He didn’t think the thing he was supposed to do was exactly nice, but he was pretty sure it wasn’t anything totally gross, either. Just a...a…<br /><br /><i>Just a prank,</i> a voice whispered in his mind, and he saw the eyes of Mr. Gaunt--dark blue, like the sea on a clear day, and strangely soothing. <i>That’s all. Just a little prank.</i><br /><br />Yeah, just a prank, whatever it was.<br /><br />No problem.”</b><br /><br />Brian Rusk owns a lot of baseball cards, but he doesn't have a 1956 Sandy Koufax card. It has proven elusive, and wanting it has evolved from a pleasant aspiration into an impulsive, desperate need. He will do almost anything to own that card. I understand these desires, but of course, I don’t have a whispering, demanding voice in my head tormenting me. When I was baseball crazy in the 1980s and my favorite team, the Kansas City Royals, were contenders every year, I wanted nothing more than to find the 1975 rookie card of George Brett. While pining for that card, I bought package after package of the current baseball cards, hoping with every pack to find the new Brett card. In those days, I couldn’t afford books, but a couple of times a week I could afford a pack of baseball cards. It wasn’t until I left home for college and worked for a bookstore in Phoenix that I walked into a Sports Memorabilia store and bought a 1975 George Brett rookie card. I still have it. Did it mean as much as it would have to me a few years earlier? No, but it was still pretty damn cool to finally own the object I had desired for so long. <br /><br />So I understand Brian’s vulnerability when he walks into the new store in town called Needful Things and meets the enigmatic Leland Gaunt. Brian is in need, and Leland has what he needs. <br /><br />Even if you don’t know what you need, Leland Gaunt is able to sift through your hidden thoughts until he finds something that you once coveted. He also sees the lingering ghosts of everyone’s insecurities. Stoke desire, rattle the cages of self-doubt, and it becomes a maelstrom in anyone’s brain. <br /><br />I am struck by the Stephen King tagline on the front cover: <b>THE LAST CASTLE ROCK STORY.</b> Assuredly, that sounds ominous and met with a certain amount of skepticism because Castle Rock has been a fruitful place of murder, mayhem, and terrifying horror for King for most of his career. Does he feel he has squeezed every drop of blood and dread out of this town? Has he tormented and persecuted the residents of Castle Rock enough that he is finally, after one more bloodbath, going to leave them in peace? So, what is he going to do, kill the town? Stab a stake through its hideous, beating heart? Nuke it? Wipe it out with a pandemic? Drop some ominous creature in their midst who will use their own longings and evil thoughts against them? <br /><br />Hmmm,<br /><br /><b>”Because the devil’s voice is sweet to hear.”</b><br /><br />This novel has a large cast of characters, and some of them will be familiar to people who have read the other novels and stories set in Castle Rock. The two characters that I was glad to meet again are Sheriff Alan Pangborn and his deputy, Norris Ridgewick, who are also in <i>The Dark Half,</i> which is one of my favorite Stephen King novels. Leland Gaunt is another wonderfully insidious King creation and can very well be an alter ego of King. After all, King is the GOD of Castle Rock, and Gaunt plays a God-like figure, not in the cold-shoulder, Christian God type way, but more like the playful God of Norse Mythology, Loki. Gaunt is playful in the way a cat is playful with a mouse. <br /><br />Needful Things has what you need. Poverty is not a deterrent. Turn out your pockets, and let's see how many coins you have. The whole point of any transaction at Needful Things is to make each customer feel like they just received the deal of a lifetime, but also leave them feeling like they still owe Gaunt something more than money. All Gaunt requires is that you play a “fun” prank on someone else. Nothing involving violence, but something that will most definitely lead to violence. <br /><br />Oh yeah, Stevie is going to tear this town apart. <br /><br />The book may look like a door stopper to a potential reader’s critical eye, but I effortlessly read big chunks of it every time I opened the cover. As we see the fears exploited and the secrets revealed of each resident, it becomes evident that, regardless of who we are or from what walk of life we come, all people can too easily be manipulated into doing insane things. <br /><br /><b>”Alan felt sanity begin to fill him again. It was funny stuff, sanity. When it was taken away, you didn’t know it. You didn’t feel its departure. You only really knew it when it was restored, like some rare wild bird which lived and sang within you not by decree but by choice.”</b><br /><br />Can everyone reacquire their sanity in time to save themselves and Castle Rock? <br /><br />If you wish to see more of my most recent book and movie reviews, visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jeffreykeeten.com">http://www.jeffreykeeten.com</a><br />I also have a Facebook blogger page at:<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten">https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten</a> and an Instagram account <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/jeffreykeeten/">https://www.instagram.com/jeffreykeeten/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="18353262481124062382" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_600510785" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/600510785" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/600510785?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/6598986-needful-things">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Horror fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Edward by: </span>
      Mom
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer600510785" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12134266930566644650">Some authors write about king slayers. Others write about serial killers. Stephen King? He writes about fuckers capable of leveling entire towns. Whether those responsible are aliens or devils, it doesn't matter. The ride is usually a fun one. <i>Needful Things</i> is no different. It is, however, the epitome of a bloated Stephen King novel. There are entire characters herein that serve zero purpose. George T. Nelson and Frank Jewett's stories could have been left out. Ace Merrill is another pointless </span>
  <span id="freeText12134266930566644650" style="display:none">Some authors write about king slayers. Others write about serial killers. Stephen King? He writes about fuckers capable of leveling entire towns. Whether those responsible are aliens or devils, it doesn't matter. The ride is usually a fun one. <i>Needful Things</i> is no different. It is, however, the epitome of a bloated Stephen King novel. There are entire characters herein that serve zero purpose. George T. Nelson and Frank Jewett's stories could have been left out. Ace Merrill is another pointless character. I simply do not see what he added to the proceedings. I never understood why Buster couldn't do everything by himself. Even when those two split up, they're still only across the street from one another. Even the movie version cut Ace and nobody cared. I theorize that Ace was a loose end for King, the bad guy that got away, so he felt the urge to give the hood a proper send off. Insert Ace in <i>Needful Things</i>. Problem solved.<br /><br />Now I know what you're thinking. "Doesn't sound like you enjoyed this one, E." Well, that's not entirely true. Yeah, I think certain characters are useless and some scenes are pointless, but I dig this book quite a bit. King always impresses me with how he manages to create entire fictional towns populated with such true-to-life personalities and make it seem so fucking effortless. At this point in his career (1991), King had killed two small towns and crippled another three: 'Salem's Lot was sucked dry; Chamberlain was never the same after Carrie White; Derry died a special kind of death but refused to go away completely; Haven would be off-limits for decades; and Castle Rock had one bombastic enima. I remain in awe of that fact. Think about that. In less than fifteen years, one author populated and then ravaged five small towns. And we loved every minute of it.<br /><br />I think several things make readers ignore the bloat in <i>Needful Things</i>. Cora and Myra's Elvis Presley fascination is awfully hilarious, as well as some of the shenanigans other characters get into. The beshitted picture of one townie's mother had me in tears, I was laughing so hard. Buster was blissfully insane, and Nettie and Wilma's fight scene is one of the most gruesome in all of horror literature. This novel is jampacked with awesome occurrences, and that makes the bloat feel worth it. Even the uber goofy ending can be ignored because the rest of the book is... well, it's just a shitload of fun. <br /><br />Obvious Tie-ins:<br /><i>The Dark Half</i><br /><i>The Body</i><br /><i>The Sun Dog</i><br /><br />Hidden Gems:<br />Gaunt refers to the items in his shop as "gray things", which supports my theory that all of King's works can be tied back to the Dark Tower series by way of <i>The Tommyknockers</i> or <i>IT</i>. I believe all of King's supernatural villains, all of his monsters, belong to the race of Old Ones known as the Prim. But more on that in my <i>A Decade with King: (1985-1994)</i> post coming in April.<br /><br />Notable Names:<br />Pop Merrill<br />Ace Merrill<br />Evvie Chalmers (I love how this woman is in five different King books, but is never on-camera, as it were)<br />George Bannerman<br />Thad Beaumont <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(This poor fucker made it through <i>The Dark Half</i> only to have one of the longest off-camera downward spirals King has written. It's mentioned here that Thad's wife leaves him and takes the kids with her, and then, ten years later in <i>Bag of Bones</i>, King mentions how Thad ended up killing himself. Poor guy.) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />In summation: It's not the best book King has ever written, but it's far, far, <i>far</i> from his worst. <i>Needful Things</i> is a favorite for many King fans, and I understand why. I simply think he could have used fewer characters to the same end. Well worth a read, whether you're a King fan or not. But, be forewarned. Whole sections of this book make no sense unless you've read <i>The Dark Half</i>.<br /><br /><b>Final Judgment: Town slaying, like a boss.</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12134266930566644650" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2735488073" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer6515362817768041071"><b>Fantastic!! What an awesome book by <i>Stephen King</i>!</b><br/><br/><b>Needful Things</b> has been on my to-read list for years. In fact, I’ve wanted to read this book for at least 10 years now.<br/><br/>One of the draws this book had for me was it was one of the first books that <i>King</i> wrote after getting clean.<br/><br/>Was he still creative? Does he still have it after the booze and cocaine?<br/>I’m here to tell you that he does, and he did in this one!<br/><br/>In fact, the ending of this book felt more finished then in other great books he wrote when h</span>
  <span id="freeText6515362817768041071" style="display:none"><b>Fantastic!! What an awesome book by <i>Stephen King</i>!</b><br /><br /><b>Needful Things</b> has been on my to-read list for years. In fact, I’ve wanted to read this book for at least 10 years now.<br /><br />One of the draws this book had for me was it was one of the first books that <i>King</i> wrote after getting clean.<br /><br />Was he still creative? Does he still have it after the booze and cocaine?<br />I’m here to tell you that he does, and he did in this one!<br /><br />In fact, the ending of this book felt more finished then in other great books he wrote when he was self-medicating. I’m looking at you <b>It</b>!<br /><br /><b>Needful Things</b> is about Castle Rock and the people that live in this town. It’s an unassuming town and has its typical issues that most all small towns have.<br />Gossip, religious competition, who got arrested last night, etc.<br /><br /><b>But one day, a new store opens in Castle Rock.</b><br /><br />And this store can give you exactly what you “think” you need.<br /><br />Enter Leland Gaunt, the owner of “Needful Things”.<br />He’s a charismatic man that will cure you with your broken heart, your crippled body or sale you something that happens to be a memory of one of the happiest days in your life.<br /><br />So please enter "Needful Things" and Leland will take care of all of your needs.<br /><br /><b>Needful Things</b> has fantastic characters that I will remember for years to come. It also has a excellent plot and epic ending.<br />The ending of the book felt right and I really loved how <i>King</i> brings the good vs evil together for a satisfying ending and fight.<br />There are moments in this book that are so brutal and descriptive.<br /><i>King</i> has a way of writing horror that just keeps building and building. The dread and anxiety just keeps escalating until it just…<b>SNAPS</b>.<br /><br /><b>I highly recommend this book to fans of <i>Stephen King</i> along with anyone that loves the horror genre. Go pick up this door stopper and get to it today!</b></span>

  <span id="freeText715220401828108896" style="display:none">King writes small town claustrophobic so well, the idea of a shop that sells any item that a customer need for just the smallest of price is a great Pack with the Devil tale.<br /><br />Set in Castle Rock this story is bursting with Easter eggs as shop owner Leland Gaunt of the recently opened ‘Needful Things’ slowly manipulates the town against each other.<br /><br />It’s a great take on materialistic items and the price people are willing to pay for that ‘must have’ item, whilst exploring the effect of one or two small incidents can slowly snowball into something bigger.<br /><br />It’s one of my favourite King stories, a great good vs evil battle along with at the time a final hurrah around Castle Rock.</span>

<div id="review_2496249177" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2496249177" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2496249177?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781501143786" href="/book/show/29430665-needful-things">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2496249177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8445130830441408275">I lost count of how many SK books I've read. However, almost all of them are brilliant and the ones that aren't brilliant are still incredibly good. Especially for someone who likes the supernatural as much as dark humour and blood. *evil cackle*<br/><br/>In this standalone story, we're in the (in-)famous town of Castle Rock in Maine. A new shop will be opened shortly, named Needful Things. Avid readers of the author will recognize the shop owner <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[as I'm pretty sure he's one of the avatars o</span></span>
  <span id="freeText8445130830441408275" style="display:none">I lost count of how many SK books I've read. However, almost all of them are brilliant and the ones that aren't brilliant are still incredibly good. Especially for someone who likes the supernatural as much as dark humour and blood. *evil cackle*<br /><br />In this standalone story, we're in the (in-)famous town of Castle Rock in Maine. A new shop will be opened shortly, named Needful Things. Avid readers of the author will recognize the shop owner <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[as I'm pretty sure he's one of the avatars of Randall Flagg / The Man in Black <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br />Anyway, the shop starts selling special items to the townspeople for practically nothing ... plus a prank. And it's these pranks that start the downfall of the town and its people (though the foundations have been there before Mr. Gaunt opened his shop).<br /><br />The premise is very simple but the author took his time to introduce us to the people populating Castle Rock as well as their connections. This was important to set the scene for what was to come once Gaunt's magic started working. <br />From little kids with terrible parents, sick but very nice people and their cooks, to town drunks, gamblers and pedophiles - we got everything here. Once again, SK shows us that the true horror lies in the ordinary. I mean <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a cocaine-addicted pedophile as a school principal and a gambling town head selectman <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, to say nothing of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the "kinky" sex fantasies of obese Cora and her friend/rival Myra <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. And those are the "ordinary" people. <br /><br />This book had a wonderful writing style. One might expect the beginning to drag due to the introductions, but King managed to sweep us along with the mystery of the shop and Mr. Gaunt right from the start. The relationships between the characters were peppered throughout to spice things up (a bit like gossip, which went very well with the small town setting and feel of this). Thus, what started as harmless pranks that seriously made me laugh soon turned not just ugly but extremely violent - not that I didn't laugh about that as well. ;P<br /><br />There are some truly shocking moments, such as when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Brian kills himself <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Sure, by the time it happens, there was enough foreshadowing already so it wasn't actually surprising per se, but it is still a blow. After all, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[he's just a boy <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. However, I must admit that I generally like that nobody is safe in SK's stories as it adds that little bit of dark realism to the mix and makes you truly be afraid for everybody, no matter who you happen to be rooting for. Also, it lets the reader feel just how high the stakes really are (too often I feel like the threat isn't actually all that bad in stories as authors don't dare going to certain places - not so with SK).<br />The other thing I always enjoy in SK's stories is the journey of discovery of the supernatural element (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[which, in this case, also leads to Pangborn being able to defeat Gaunt <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>). And that didn't disappoint here, either. <br /><br />One other really neat thing I enjoyed was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that the end was almost word for word the same as the beginning <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> - that was especially nice, stylistically. <br /><br />It took me a long time to read this book (it was meant as the final read in Spooktober) but not because of the book itself (some people will know just how bad 2020 has gotten for me by the end of last month). Sorry to my buddy-readers, Dennis and Brad, it really wasn't my fault.<br />I can honestly say that this book now ranks high up there with <b>Pet Sematary</b> and <b>It</b> as one of my favourite stories by this author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8445130830441408275" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3546817423?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jilly" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly">Jilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

<span id="freeTextContainer14951685323065367651">I'm just sayin' if you live in a small town in Maine, you should expect to be killed by some sort of paranormal fuckery. I don't make the rules.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600231684i/30112374.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This one is set in Castle Rock which is near where Cujo guarded Shawshank Prison or whatever.   <span id="freeText14951685323065367651" style="display:none">I'm just sayin' if you live in a small town in Maine, you should expect to be killed by some sort of paranormal fuckery. I don't make the rules.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600231684i/30112374.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This one is set in Castle Rock which is near where Cujo guarded Shawshank Prison or whatever. Literally dying.. .buwahaha!<br><br>Okay, not right away. The way Stephen King works is to invest you in all of the gazillion characters so that it hurts more when they die. He's such a sadist.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1600231684ra/30112375.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Our most invested-in person is the sheriff, who of course has a horrible back-story of tragedy and loss. Missed out on that fun!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600231684i/30112372._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But, everyone else has their not-even-good-enough-for-ebay crap, I mean <i>treasures</i> that they must hold on to and never share with anyone ever!!!! It was compelling and there was enough bloody killing to satisfy any <s>sadistic fuck</s> horror book lover. <br><br>Read this one!<br>Oh, but keep in mind that it has pretty much ALL the triggers. So, maybe don't read this one. It's up to you. I'm not your mother.</span>

<div id="review_380756248" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/380756248" />
    <a title="Nicholas Armstrong" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2593734-nicholas-armstrong"><img alt="Nicholas Armstrong" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1284413844p2/2593734.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/380756248?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicholas Armstrong" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicholas Armstrong" href="/user/show/2593734-nicholas-armstrong">Nicholas Armstrong</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer380756248" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4717538185043654769">I was going to say that the reason I didn't like this book was the huge cast of characters, but that isn't true. Sure, the huge cast bothered me, but I've read books like that before, the problem was far more to do with the writing. The writing was belabored, tired, and trite. I say this with the utmost respect for King, but it was.<br/><br/>For example, the huge cast of characters followed a largely identical format. With a book rocking 730 or so pages of small font, that's a lot of reading, and, as with</span>
  <span id="freeText4717538185043654769" style="display:none">I was going to say that the reason I didn't like this book was the huge cast of characters, but that isn't true. Sure, the huge cast bothered me, but I've read books like that before, the problem was far more to do with the writing. The writing was belabored, tired, and trite. I say this with the utmost respect for King, but it was.<br /><br />For example, the huge cast of characters followed a largely identical format. With a book rocking 730 or so pages of small font, that's a lot of reading, and, as with <i>Atlas Shrugged</i>, it had better be worth it. But it wasn't. Scenes were repeated, almost identically, with different characters. A dozen characters marched into Needful Things, had a nearly identical conversation with Leland Gaunt, and then marched out. Different characters vandalized cars and I had to watch them both. Even though they were there for the same reason, doing the same thing, and it was largely the exact same scene. THAT was the problem with <i>Needful Things</i>. It was that the book was extremely repetitive with no payoff.<br /><br />Additionally, the end was far, far too gimicky. The ending was just a variation of riding off into the sunset but with the identical language that every other book/movie uses. "what happened?" "we'll never know" blah, blah, blah. I know endings are hard, I really do, but using a cliche one is not okay. Use a variation, spice it up, do something new. To top it off, the final, final, ending was the end of 90% of horror movies "Is it REALLY over?" It was unnecessary. It added nothing, and it didn't improve the story or development.<br /><br />Sorry to say, but this is the worst King book I've read, and I really hope it is the worst of them all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4717538185043654769" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
